      <p>
       The
       <b>
        British Overseas Territories
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        BOT
       </b>
       ) or alternatively,
       <b>
        United Kingdom's Overseas Territories
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        UKOTs
       </b>
       ), are 14
       <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">
        territories
       </a>
       under the jurisdiction and sovereignty of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fco_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fco-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They are the parts of the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       that have not been granted independence or have voted to remain British territories. These territories do not form part of the United Kingdom and, with the exception of Gibraltar, are not part of the European Union. Most of the inhabited territories are internally self-governing, with the UK retaining responsibility for defence and foreign relations. The rest are either uninhabited or have a transitory population of military or scientific personnel. They share the
       <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">
        British monarch
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Elizabeth II
       </a>
       ) as
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The term "British Overseas Territory" was introduced by the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_Act_2002" title="British Overseas Territories Act 2002">
        British Overseas Territories Act 2002
       </a>
       , replacing the term
       <i>
        British Dependent Territory
       </i>
       , introduced by the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Nationality_Act_1981" title="British Nationality Act 1981">
        British Nationality Act 1981
       </a>
       . Prior to 1 January 1983, the territories were officially referred to as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">
         British Crown Colonies
        </a>
       </i>
       . With the exceptions of the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">
        British Antarctic Territory
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">
        South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands
       </a>
       (which host only officials and research station staff) and the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">
        British Indian Ocean Territory
       </a>
       (used as a military base), the Territories retain permanent civilian populations. Permanent residency for the 7,000 or so civilians living in the Sovereign Base Areas of
       <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">
        Akrotiri and Dhekelia
       </a>
       is limited to citizens of the Republic of
       <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Collectively, the Territories encompass a population of about 250,000 people and a land area of about 1,727,570 square kilometres (667,020 sq mi). The vast majority of this land area, 1,700,000 square kilometres (660,000 sq mi), constitutes the almost uninhabited British Antarctic Territory, while the largest territory by population, Bermuda, accounts for almost a quarter of the total BOT population. At the other end of the scale, three territories have no civilian population; the Antarctic territory, the British Indian Ocean Territory (from which the Chagos Islanders were controversially removed) and South Georgia.
       <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">
        Pitcairn Islands
       </a>
       , settled by the survivors of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty">
        Mutiny on the Bounty
       </a>
       , is the smallest settled territory with 49 inhabitants, while the smallest by land area is Gibraltar on the southern tip of the Iberian peninsula.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The United Kingdom participates in the
       <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">
        Antarctic Treaty System
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and, as part of a mutual agreement, the British Antarctic Territory is recognised by four of the six other
       <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_Antarctica" title="Territorial claims in Antarctica">
        sovereign nations making claims to Antarctic territory
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">
        Crown dependencies
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">
        Jersey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">
        Guernsey
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">
        Isle of Man
       </a>
       are also under the
       <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
        sovereignty
       </a>
       of the British monarch, they are in a different constitutional relationship with the United Kingdom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The British Overseas Territories and Crown Dependencies are themselves distinct from the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">
        Commonwealth realms
       </a>
       , a group of 15 independent countries (and the United Kingdom) each having Elizabeth II as their reigning monarch, and from the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        Commonwealth of Nations
       </a>
       , a voluntary association of 52 countries mostly with historic links to the British Empire (which also includes all Commonwealth realms).
      </p>
      <p>
       As of August 2014
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Minister responsible for the Territories excluding the
       <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">
        Falkland Islands
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       and the Sovereign Base Areas is
       <a href="/wiki/Tariq_Ahmad,_Baron_Ahmad_of_Wimbledon" title="Tariq Ahmad, Baron Ahmad of Wimbledon">
        Tariq Ahmad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">
        Minister of State for the Commonwealth and the UN
       </a>
       . The other three territories are the responsibility of Sir
       <a href="/wiki/Alan_Duncan" title="Alan Duncan">
        Alan Duncan
       </a>
       MP,
       <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_for_Foreign_Affairs_(United_Kingdom)" title="Minister of State for Foreign Affairs (United Kingdom)">
        Minister of State for Europe and the Americas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_overseas_territories">
        Current overseas territories

       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_that_have_gained_independence_from_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of countries that have gained independence from the United Kingdom">
        List of countries that have gained independence from the United Kingdom
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="337" data-file-width="450" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg/250px-Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg/375px-Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bermuda-Harbour_and_Town_of_St_George.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George's, Bermuda">
          St. George's
         </a>
         town, in the Islands of Bermuda, or "The Somers Isles". The colony was founded by the wrecking of the flagship of the
         <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">
          Virginia Company
         </a>
         in 1609. The Company's charter was extended to include Bermuda in 1612, and it has remained a British colony ever since. Since the rebellion of
         <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">
          Virginia
         </a>
         , it has been the oldest-remaining British colony, and the town of St. George's is the oldest continuously inhabited British settlement in the New World.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smithsonian_32-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-Smithsonian-32">
           [32]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Early colonies, in the sense of English subjects residing in lands hitherto outside the control of the English government, were generally known as "
       <a href="/wiki/Plantation_(settlement_or_colony)" title="Plantation (settlement or colony)">
        Plantations
       </a>
       ".
      </p>
      <p>
       The first, unofficial, colony was
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">
        Newfoundland
       </a>
       , where English fishermen routinely set up seasonal camps in the 16th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is now a province of Canada known as Newfoundland and Labrador. It retains strong cultural ties with Britain.
      </p>
      <p>
       English colonisation of North America began officially in 1607 with the settlement of
       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown,_Virginia" title="Jamestown, Virginia">
        Jamestown
       </a>
       , the first successful permanent colony in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_and_Dominion_of_Virginia" title="Colony and Dominion of Virginia">
        Virginia
       </a>
       (a term that was then applied generally to North America). Its offshoot, Bermuda, was settled inadvertently after the wrecking of the Virginia company's flagship there in 1609, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Company" title="Virginia Company">
        Virginia Company
       </a>
       's charter extended to officially include the archipelago in 1612.
       <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s,_Bermuda" title="St. George's, Bermuda">
        St. George's
       </a>
       town, founded in Bermuda in that year, remains the oldest continuously inhabited British settlement in the New World (with some historians stating that – its formation predating the 1619 conversion of "James Fort" into "Jamestown" – St. George's was actually the first successful town the English established in the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       ). Bermuda and Bermudians have played important, sometimes pivotal, but generally underestimated or unacknowledged roles in the shaping of the English and British trans-Atlantic Empires. These include maritime commerce, settlement of the continent and of the West Indies, and the projection of naval power via the colony's
       <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">
        privateers
       </a>
       , among other areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The growth of the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
        British Empire
       </a>
       in the 19th century, to its territorial peak in the 1920s, saw Britain acquire nearly one quarter of the world's land mass, including territories with large indigenous populations in Asia and Africa. From the mid-nineteenth century to the early twentieth century, the larger settler colonies – in Canada, Australia, New Zealand and South Africa – first became
       <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">
        self-governing colonies
       </a>
       and then achieved independence in all matters except foreign policy, defence and trade. Separate self-governing colonies federated to become Canada (in 1867), Australia (in 1901), South Africa (in 1910), and Rhodesia (in 1965). These and other large self-governing colonies had become known as
       <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">
        Dominions
       </a>
       by the 1920s. The Dominions achieved almost full independence with the
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">
        Statute of Westminster (1931)
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_in_its_region_(North_America_special).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="233" data-file-width="415" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_in_its_region_%28North_America_special%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_in_its_region_(North_America_special).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Many of the overseas territories are in the Caribbean, as shown on the map.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Through a process of
       <a href="/wiki/British_Empire#Decolonisation_and_decline_(1945–1997)" title="British Empire">
        decolonisation
       </a>
       following the Second World War, most of the British colonies in Africa, Asia and the Caribbean gained independence. Some colonies became
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">
        Commonwealth realms
       </a>
       , retaining the British monarch as their own
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most former colonies and protectorates became
       <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Member states of the Commonwealth of Nations">
        member states of the Commonwealth of Nations
       </a>
       , a non-political,
       <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_association" title="Voluntary association">
        voluntary association
       </a>
       of equal members, comprising a population of around 2.2 billion people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the independence of
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">
        Southern Rhodesia
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
        Zimbabwe
       </a>
       ) in Africa in 1980 and
       <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">
        British Honduras
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       ) in Central America in 1981, the last major colony that remained was
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       , with a population of over 5 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With 1997 approaching, the United Kingdom and China negotiated the
       <a href="/wiki/Sino-British_Joint_Declaration" title="Sino-British Joint Declaration">
        Sino-British Joint Declaration
       </a>
       , which led to the whole of Hong Kong becoming a "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_administrative_region_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" title="Special administrative region (People's Republic of China)">
        special administrative region
       </a>
       " of China in 1997, subject to various conditions intended to guarantee the preservation of Hong Kong's capitalist economy and its way of life under British rule for at least
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Basic_Law" title="Hong Kong Basic Law">
        50 years after the handover
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/George_Town,_Cayman_Islands" title="George Town, Cayman Islands">
        George Town
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
        Cayman Islands
       </a>
       has consequently become the largest city in the Overseas Territories.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2002, the British Parliament passed the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_Act_2002" title="British Overseas Territories Act 2002">
        British Overseas Territories Act 2002
       </a>
       . This reclassified the UK's dependent territories as
       <i>
        overseas territories
       </i>
       and, with the exception of those people solely connected with the Sovereign Base Areas of Cyprus, restored full British citizenship to their inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McKeeva_Bush,_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg/220px-McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg/330px-McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg/440px-McKeeva_Bush%2C_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McKeeva_Bush,_Premier_of_the_Cayman_Islands_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/McKeeva_Bush" title="McKeeva Bush">
          McKeeva Bush
         </a>
         , Premier of the
         <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
          Cayman Islands
         </a>
         in 2012
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Head_of_state">
        Head of state
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Head of state">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (February 2011)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The head of state in the overseas territories is the British monarch, Elizabeth II. The Queen's role in the territories is in her role as Queen of the United Kingdom, and not in right of each territory.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Queen appoints a representative in each territory to exercise her executive power. In territories with a permanent population, a Governor is appointed by the Queen on the advice of the British Government, usually a retired senior military officer,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       or a senior civil servant. In territories without a permanent population, a Commissioner is usually appointed to represent the Queen. Exceptionally, in the overseas territory of Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha, an Administrator is appointed to be the Governor's representative in each of the two distant parts of the territory, namely
       <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">
        Ascension Island
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">
        Tristan da Cunha
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The role of the Governor is to act as the
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
        head of state
       </a>
       , and they are usually responsible for appointing the head of government, and senior political positions in the territory. The Governor is also responsible for liaising with the UK Government, and carrying out any ceremonial duties. A Commissioner has the same powers as a Governor, but also acts as the head of government.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">
        Local government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Local government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_heads_of_government_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_dependencies#Overseas_Territories" title="List of current heads of government in the United Kingdom and dependencies">
        List of current heads of government in the United Kingdom and dependencies § Overseas Territories
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_dependent_territories" title="List of leaders of dependent territories">
        List of leaders of dependent territories
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       All the overseas territories have their own system of government, and localised laws. The structure of the government appears to be closely correlated to the size and political development of the territory.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Territories
        </th>
        <th>
         Government
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">
            British Antarctic Territory
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">
            South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         There is no native or permanent population; therefore there is no elected government. The Commissioner, supported by an Administrator, run the affairs of the territory.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">
            British Indian Ocean Territory
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         There is no elected government, as there is no native settled population. The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chagossian" title="Chagossian">
          Chagos Islanders
         </a>
         – who were forcibly evicted from the territory in 1971 – won a
         <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">
          High Court
         </a>
         Judgement allowing them to return, but this was then overridden by an
         <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">
          Order in Council
         </a>
         preventing them from returning. The final appeal to the
         <a href="/wiki/Judicial_functions_of_the_House_of_Lords" title="Judicial functions of the House of Lords">
          House of Lords
         </a>
         (regarding the lawfulness of the Order in Council) was decided in the government's favour, exhausting the islanders' legal options in the United Kingdom at present.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">
            Akrotiri and Dhekelia
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         There is no elected government. The Commander British Forces Cyprus acts as the territory's Administrator, with a Chief Officer responsible for day-to-day running of the civil government. As far as possible, there is convergence of laws
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
            <span title='Convergence is dynamic, but this is probably meant to refer to a static condition. Should this read "... the laws are consistent with those of the Republic of Cyprus" or "... the laws are written to conform with those of the Republic of Cyprus"? (April 2017)'>
             clarification needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
         with those of the Republic of Cyprus.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Islands" title="Pitcairn Islands">
            Pitcairn Islands
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         There are an elected
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_the_Pitcairn_Islands" title="List of rulers of the Pitcairn Islands">
          Mayor
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Island_Council_(Pitcairn)" title="Island Council (Pitcairn)">
          Island Council
         </a>
         , who have the power to propose and administer local legislation. However, their decisions are subject to approval by the Governor, who retains near-unlimited powers of plenary legislation on behalf of the United Kingdom Government.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">
            Falkland Islands
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         The Government consists of an elected
         <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="Legislative Assembly of the Falkland Islands">
          Legislative Assembly
         </a>
         , with the
         <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="Chief Executive of the Falkland Islands">
          Chief Executive
         </a>
         and the Director of Corporate Resources as
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio">
           ex officio
          </a>
         </i>
         members.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
          <a href="#cite_note-40">
           [40]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">
            Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         The Government consists of an elected Legislative Council. The Governor is the head of government and leads the Executive Council, consisting of appointed members made up from the Legislative Council and two
         <i>
          ex-officio
         </i>
         members. Governance on Ascension Island and Tristan da Cunha is led by Administrators who are advised by elected Island Councils.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
          <a href="#cite_note-41">
           [41]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">
            Anguilla
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">
            British Virgin Islands
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
            Cayman Islands
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">
            Montserrat
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         These territories have a House of Assembly, Legislative Assembly (Cayman Islands), or Legislative Council (Montserrat) with political parties. The Executive Council is usually called a cabinet and is led by a
         <a href="/wiki/Premier" title="Premier">
          Premier
         </a>
         or a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" title="Chief Minister">
          Chief Minister
         </a>
         (in Anguilla), who is the leader of the majority party in parliament. The Governor exercises less power over local affairs and deals mostly with foreign affairs and economic issues, while the elected government controls most "domestic" concerns.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
            Gibraltar
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         Under the
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">
          Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006
         </a>
         which was approved in Gibraltar by
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_constitutional_referendum,_2006" title="Gibraltarian constitutional referendum, 2006">
          a referendum
         </a>
         , Gibraltar now has a
         <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">
          Parliament
         </a>
         . The
         <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">
          Government of Gibraltar
         </a>
         , headed by the
         <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">
          Chief Minister
         </a>
         , is elected. Defence, external affairs and internal security vest in the
         <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Gibraltar" title="Governor of Gibraltar">
          Governor
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
          <a href="#cite_note-42">
           [42]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">
            Bermuda
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         Bermuda, settled in 1609, and self-governed since 1620, is the oldest and most populous of the Overseas Territories. The bicameral
         <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Bermuda" title="Parliament of Bermuda">
          Parliament
         </a>
         consists of a
         <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Bermuda" title="Senate of Bermuda">
          Senate
         </a>
         and a
         <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Bermuda" title="House of Assembly of Bermuda">
          House of Assembly
         </a>
         , and most executive powers have been devolved to the head of government, known as the
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premiers_of_Bermuda" title="List of Premiers of Bermuda">
          Premier
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">
            Turks and Caicos Islands
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </td>
        <td>
         The Turks and Caicos Islands adopted a new constitution effective 9 August 2006; their head of government now also has the title
         <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Premier of the Turks and Caicos Islands">
          Premier
         </a>
         , their legislature is called the House of Assembly, and their autonomy has been greatly increased.
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">
             citation needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">
        Legal system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Legal system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #ededed">
         <span class="fn org">
          British Overseas Territories Joint Ministerial Council
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #ededed">
         Type
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Type
        </th>
        <td>
         <div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.3em;">
          <span class="category">
           Dialogue forum
          </span>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Seats
        </th>
        <td>
         28-30
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #ededed">
         Elections
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voting_system" title="Voting system">
           Voting system
          </a>
         </div>
        </th>
        <td>
         All members elected either as MPs in the UK cabinet or as heads of Government or Ministers in Overseas Territories.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #ededed">
         Meeting place
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td class="label" colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">
          Westminster
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
          London
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #ededed">
         Website
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <span class="url">
          <a class="external text" href="https://www.gov.uk/government/topical-events/overseas-territories-joint-ministerial-council" rel="nofollow">
           www
           <wbr/>
           .gov
           <wbr/>
           .uk
           <wbr/>
           /government
           <wbr/>
           /topical-events
           <wbr/>
           /overseas-territories-joint-ministerial-council
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Each overseas territory has its own legal system independent of the United Kingdom. The legal system is generally based on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_common_law" title="English common law">
        English common law
       </a>
       , with some distinctions for local circumstances. Each territory has its own attorney general, and court system. For the smaller territories, the UK may appoint a UK-based lawyer or judge to work on legal cases. This is particularly important for cases involving serious crimes and where it is impossible to find a jury who will not know the defendant in a small population island.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_sexual_assault_trial_of_2004" title="Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004">
        Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004
       </a>
       is an example of how the UK may choose to provide the legal framework for particular cases where the territory cannot do so alone.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_Ministerial_Council">
        Joint Ministerial Council
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Joint Ministerial Council">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A joint ministerial council of UK ministers, and the leaders of the Overseas Territories has been held annually since 2012 to provide representation between UK Government departments and Overseas Territory Governments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_the_United_Kingdom">
        Relations with the United Kingdom
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Relations with the United Kingdom">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1424" data-file-width="2136" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg/250px-British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg/375px-British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg/500px-British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Overseas_Territories_Joint_Ministerial_Council_with_Cameron.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Leaders of the Overseas Territories with former Prime Minister
         <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">
          David Cameron
         </a>
         in 2012.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tristanfromspace.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1440" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tristanfromspace.jpg/250px-Tristanfromspace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tristanfromspace.jpg/375px-Tristanfromspace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tristanfromspace.jpg/500px-Tristanfromspace.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tristanfromspace.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">
          Tristan da Cunha
         </a>
         on 6 February 2013, as seen from space. The population was temporarily evacuated to the UK in 1961 because of an eruption. Postal code TDCU 1ZZ
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg/250px-Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg/375px-Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg/500px-Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_Montserrat.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Coastline at Little Bay, the site of the new capital of Montserrat replacing
         <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">
          Plymouth
         </a>
         . The project is funded by the
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
          <a href="#cite_note-44">
           [44]
          </a>
         </sup>
         UK's
         <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">
          Department for International Development
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:British_Overseas_Territories_(at_the_same_geographic_scale).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="745" data-file-width="771" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg/220px-British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg/330px-British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg/440px-British_Overseas_Territories_%28at_the_same_geographic_scale%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:British_Overseas_Territories_(at_the_same_geographic_scale).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         British Overseas Territories at the same geographic scale as the UK.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">
        Foreign and Commonwealth Office
       </a>
       (FCO) has the responsibility of looking after the interests of all overseas territories except the Sovereign Base Areas of Akrotiri and Dhekelia, which comes under the jurisdiction of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">
        Ministry of Defence
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Within the FCO, the general responsibility for the territories is handled by the Overseas Territories Directorate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2012, the FCO published
       <i>
        The Overseas Territories: security, success and sustainability
       </i>
       which set out Britain's policy for the Overseas Territories, covering six main areas:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Defence, security and safety of the territories and their people
       </li>
       <li>
        Successful and resilient economies
       </li>
       <li>
        Cherishing the environment
       </li>
       <li>
        Making government work better
       </li>
       <li>
        Vibrant and flourishing communities
       </li>
       <li>
        Productive links with the wider world
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Britain and the overseas territories do not have diplomatic representations, although the governments of the overseas territories with indigenous populations all retain a representative office in London. The United Kingdom Overseas Territories Association (UKOTA) also represents the interests of the territories in London. The governments in both London and territories occasionally meet to mitigate or resolve disagreements over the process of governance in the territories and levels of autonomy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Britain provides financial assistance to the overseas territories via the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">
        Department for International Development
       </a>
       . Currently
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2010)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       only Montserrat and Saint Helena receive budgetary aid (i.e. financial contribution to recurrent funding).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Several specialist funds are made available by the UK, including:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The Good Government Fund which provides assistance on government administration;
       </li>
       <li>
        The Economic Diversification Programme Budget which aim to diversify and enhance the economic bases of the territories.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The territories have no official representation in the UK Parliament, but have informal representation through the All-Party Parliamentary Group,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and can
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epetition" title="Epetition">
        petition
       </a>
       the UK Government through the
       <a href="/wiki/Directgov" title="Directgov">
        Directgov
       </a>
       e-Petitions website.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Only
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       has representation in the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">
        European Parliament
       </a>
       and it shares its Member with the region of
       <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">
        South West England
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Two national parties,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UKIP" title="UKIP">
        UKIP
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">
        Liberal Democrats
       </a>
       , have endorsed calls for direct representation of overseas territories in the UK Parliament, as well as backbench members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">
        Conservative Party
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">
        Labour Party
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs">
        Foreign affairs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign affairs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">
        Special member state territories and the European Union
       </a>
      </div>

          </a>
         </div>
         Gibraltar is the only overseas territory included in the European Union
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Foreign affairs of the overseas territories are handled by the FCO in London. Some territories maintain diplomatic officers in nearby countries for trade and immigration purposes. Several of the territories in the Americas maintain membership within the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">
        Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">
        Caribbean Community
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Development_Bank" title="Caribbean Development Bank">
        Caribbean Development Bank
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency">
        Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">
        Association of Caribbean States
       </a>
       . The territories are members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">
        Commonwealth of Nations
       </a>
       through the United Kingdom. The inhabited territories compete in their own right at the
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">
        Commonwealth Games
       </a>
       , and three of the territories (
       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">
        Bermuda
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
        Cayman Islands
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">
        British Virgin Islands
       </a>
       ) sent teams to the
       <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">
        2008 Summer Olympics
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
        Gibraltar
       </a>
       is the only overseas territory that is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       (EU), although it is not part of the European Customs Union, the European Tax Policy, the European Statistics Zone or the Common Agriculture Policy. Gibraltar is not a member of the European Union in its own right. The Sovereign Base Areas in Cyprus are not part of the European Union, but they are the only British overseas territory to use the euro as official currency. None of the other Overseas Territories are members of the EU, the main body of EU law does not apply and, although certain slices of EU law are applied to those territories as part of the EU's Association of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_Countries_and_Territories" title="Overseas Countries and Territories">
        Overseas Countries and Territories
       </a>
       (OCT Association), they are not commonly enforceable in local courts. The OCT Association also provides overseas territories with structural funding for regeneration projects.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the return of full
       <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">
        British citizenship
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to most 'belongers' of overseas territories (mainly since the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories_Act_2002" title="British Overseas Territories Act 2002">
        British Overseas Territories Act 2002
       </a>
       ), the citizens of those territories hold concurrent European Union citizenship, giving them rights of free movement across all EU member states.
      </p>
      <p>
       Several nations dispute the UK's sovereignty in the following overseas territories:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Akrotiri_and_Dhekelia" title="Akrotiri and Dhekelia">
         Akrotiri and Dhekelia
        </a>
        – claimed by
        <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">
         Cyprus
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Territory" title="British Antarctic Territory">
         British Antarctic Territory
        </a>
        – Territory overlaps Antarctic claims made by
        <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
         Chile
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
         Argentina
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">
         British Indian Ocean Territory
        </a>
        – claimed by
        <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">
         Mauritius
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">
         Seychelles
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">
         Falkland Islands
        </a>
        – claimed by
        <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
         Argentina
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
         Gibraltar
        </a>
        – claimed by Spain
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/South_Georgia_and_the_South_Sandwich_Islands" title="South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands">
         South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands
        </a>
        – claimed by
        <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
         Argentina
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Citizenship">
        Citizenship
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Overseas_Territories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Citizenship">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">

          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Tone" role="presentation">

           </a>
           used on Wikipedia
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           See Wikipedia's
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">
            guide to writing better articles
           </a>
           for suggestions.
          </span>

           <i>
            (February 2015)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>

           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
